## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor concentration–time dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard state-variable form for chemical kinetics ODEs in a well-mixed (batch) system. Typical relationships express dA_dt as a rate law depending on A (and sometimes explicitly on t via catalysts, forcing, or time-varying conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption of A, e.g., saturated catalyst)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or dimerization-limited decay)
- General n-th order rate law (power-law): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global kinetics over a regime)
- Autocatalytic growth/decay: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (logistic-like kinetics from growth with depletion/inhibition)
- Reversible first-order to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (approach to nonzero steady state A_ss = c1/c0)
- Reversible-like with explicit equilibrium concentration: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Time-modulated first-order (time-varying rate coefficient): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t) * A (e.g., changing temperature/irradiation over time)
- Exponentially time-varying rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decelerating kinetics due to ramping conditions)
- Catalyst activation/deactivation forcing: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (baseline decay plus time-dependent source/sink term)
- Self-limiting/inhibited kinetics (rational form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective saturation/inhibition in the disappearance rate)
- Mixed-order (sum of pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order consumption channels)
- Signed source–sink with production and consumption: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A - c2 * A**2 (net generation with linear/quadratic losses)
- Empirical polynomial-in-A rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (local approximation of complex kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action disappearance of A → negative sign with monotone increasing magnitude in A (e.g., -c*A, -c*A**2)
- Parallel reaction pathways → additive rate contributions (sum of multiple terms in A with different orders)
- Reversible/approach-to-equilibrium behavior → linear relaxation term in (A - A_eq), giving a steady state where dA_dt = 0
- Catalyst deactivation/activation or external program → rate coefficient becomes an explicit function of t (e.g., (1+c*t), exp(c*t))
- Net production plus decay (source–sink) → constant or time-dependent source term added to concentration-dependent loss terms
- Inhibition/self-limitation → rational dependence on A that reduces effective rate at high A (e.g., A/(A+c))
- Autocatalysis with depletion → coexistence of growth-like and higher-order loss terms (c*A - c*A**2) producing an internal stable level
- Early-time transient vs late-time asymptote → models with nonzero steady state (constant term or (A-c)) rather than pure decay to zero
- Regime-dependent kinetics over limited data range → general power-law order c1 (non-integer) can fit global kinetics when mechanism is unknown

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK19)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A*exp(-c3*_s*t) + c4*_t*sin(log(A + c5))
Candidates evaluated: 57
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.16498*A² - 0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) + 0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three terms:
1. `-0.16498*A²` (polynomial in A)
2. `-0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t)` (A times exponential in t)
3. `0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))` (sin of log of (A+1))

The key basis functions are: A², A*exp(αt), and sin(log(A+1)).

**Critical observation:** The term `sin(log(A+1))` is a very specific transcendental function. For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce this exact function. Let me check which candidates can generate `sin(log(A+1))`.

Most candidates use building blocks like:
- `A*log(A*c+1)`, `A²*log(A*c+1)` — these are log-based, not sin(log(...))
- `sin(A*c + c)` — this is sin of a linear function of A, NOT sin(log(A+1))
- `log(c*exp(A*c)+1)` — this is a softplus-like function
- `A^(3/2)`, `A^3` — power functions

**sin(log(A+1))** cannot be expressed as any combination of:
- Polynomials in A
- A*log(A+c)
- A²*log(A+c)
- sin(A*c + c) (sin of linear ≠ sin of log)
- exp(A*c)
- log(A*c+1)
- A^(3/2), A^3
- Rational functions of A

These are all fundamentally different basis functions. sin(log(A+1)) is linearly independent from all of these.

Let me check **Candidate 5**: `A*c0 + A*c1*log(A*c2 + 1) + A*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*sin(c6*log(c7*exp(A*c8) + 1) + c9)`

The last term: `c5*sin(c6*log(c7*exp(A*c8) + 1) + c9)`. If c8→0, then exp(A*c8)→1+A*c8, and log(c7*(1+A*c8)+1) ≈ log(c7+1+c7*c8*A). This doesn't cleanly give log(A+1).

Actually, let me try: set c8=0, then exp(0)=1, so log(c7*1+1) = log(c7+1) = constant. That makes the sin term a constant, not sin(log(A+1)).

What if c7=1, c8 is small? log(exp(A*c8)+1) for general c8 is NOT log(A+1).

Can we get log(A+1)? We need log(c7*exp(A*c8)+1) = log(A+1). This requires c7*exp(A*c8) = A, which is impossible for all A.

**None of the candidates contain the basis function sin(log(A+c))**, which is essential for matching the GT. Every candidate uses different transcendental structures (log, sin of linear, exp, powers) that cannot reproduce sin(log(A+1)).

Let me verify each candidate systematically — all lack sin(log(·)):

Candidates 1-57: None contain `sin(log(...))` as a building block. The closest are candidates with `sin(A*c+c)` (sin of linear), `log(c*exp(A*c)+1)` (softplus), or pure polynomial/log terms. None can produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

Since sin(log(A+1)) is linearly independent from all basis functions present in any candidate, no candidate can match.
